Where I come from (Serbia), we call crapes pancakes, and I find that the easiest way to flip them is just with the pan, making a fast circle motion down away from me and back, thus tossing the crape in the air and flipping it. A easy "hack" for flipping crepes is using a glass pot lid. Cover the pan with the lid, turn it upside down, and then just slide the crape back into the pan. Oh and I try to avoid using induction cooktops for crapes, gas burners are a better fit for me when doing this.

I know I'm late but in Hungary we have crepe cake, but with totally different fillings. We make a layer of grated walnut+sugar, then a grated chocolate layer, then a marmalade layer (possibly made of apricots and not melty fake jelly) and a sweet cottage cheese layer. Repeat untill you run out of fillings or crepes. Smear sour cream to the top, sprinkle with chocolate and bake it in the oven. Also for crepe we have a totally different recipe and it's stable af.

Crepe recipe:  1/2 cup cold water 1/2 cup milk (regular milk is best) 2 cups flour (approx) pinch salt **********OPTIONAL************** two eggs 1 tablespoon butter  DIRECTIONS  PUT EVERYTHING IN A BLENDER and liquefy very briefly (45 secs)  Consistency of this thing should be a slightly more watery pancake batter.  If it's too watery, add more flour.  Definitely don't make it chunky.   Put the thing in the refrigerator at least an hour until all the bubbles disappear.  At this time, the batter will be a little thicker because it is cold and the flour will expand.  You can leave this in the refrigerator overnight so you can handle it better.   COOK Use a big ass pan with a flat bottom.  Heat to medium high to start and when ready to cook, go to medium. Spray with oil (PAM). Use a ladle to scoop this in the center and then pick up the pan to spread the crepe around as much of the pan as possible.  When the edges dry and fold up slightly, it's ready to flip it.  You flip ONCE.  Respray the pan with PAM every time you make another one.    This works EVERYTIME.  This will make about 7 to 8 crepes.  The mixing will take less than 10 minutes and the refrigerator is only an hour long.   You should be able to make and serve this within 3 hours or less.   Good luck.

Americans say crÃªpe that way because of the rules regarding stressed vowels in American English pronunciation. The French pronunciation requires an unstressed vowel in what should be a stressed syllable in English thus rendering the pronunciation very uncomfortable to the American mouth. The vowel we use normally is a diphthong that combines that original e sound with an i sound making it easier for us to pronounce.

*Rie's crepe recipe (proper recipe ehe)*  ADD ALL TOGETHER (dry ingredients) -1 and 3/4cup flour -1/4cup of coco powder -7tbsp of sugar -pinch of salt  -then add 6 eggs into dry ingredients  -then add 6 tbsp on melted butter  -then add 3 cup of milk, adding 1/2cup at a time  -then strain the batter.  -let it sit for 30 min (covered in wrapping paper)  *done! or if u wanna make the crepe cake, continue*  -whip 4 cups of cream!(until yoi get a still peak)  -make 20 crepes to assemble them into CREPES  -all you gotta do after that is ASSEMBLE THE CREPES  *how to make the ganache* -2 cups of cream into a boiler  -then add 4tbsp of sugar to the cream and mix them into the cream  -get a bowl, chop some chocolate (dark perferably since you're adding in 4 tbsp of sugar and since cream has sugar in it as well) and add them into the bowl  -slowly pour in the hot cream w/ sugar (about 1//3 of it) , count to 30 seconds then MIX  -spread it all on there nice and thick yumm  -dont forget sugar powder and sprinkle them baby on there as well

10:40 Ganache means "idiot" in french (even though we don't really use this word anymore, it's very Vieux FranÃ§ais): the legend tells us that in the middle XIXth century, a pastry chef apprentice  mistakenly pourred cream in a pot of melted chocolate. His master saw it, and called the apprentice a ganache (an idiot, a jerk). But he tasted it, just to give it a try, and was pleasantly surprised. That's why it's called a ganache.

After watching this I found myself thinking she should have realized that cocoa powder is not a replacement for flour. A food channel with people who do not think about this stuff lol. Also to the people complaining about the cook top not working correctly did you watch the whole video? After they fixed the batter everything worked out fine. The batter is made of a ratio of dry to wet ingredients. Flour and egg both contain protein which when combined with the wet help hold things together. Listen to what she says about having to let the batter rest and you realize she does not really understand how flour works in the recipe. Her ratio was off because she figured more cocoa powder was better in the recipe but, you can not sub things without understanding how they work. The cocoa powder was only needed to add a bit of color and flavor to the crepes. It does not contain anything that can help bind batter together and the result was moisture evaporating to fast (pan to hot) as well as tearing of the finished crepe (weak structure). .

Niki, you should get a little blue steel crepe pan (the edges are only about 1/2 inch high and beveled outward). They are pretty inexpensive and will save you from getting burns on your hands. I make crepes pretty often and I love mine. Btw, I do have to butter the pan just before the first crepe (which usually doesn't turn out pretty, but still tastes good), but it doesn't need butter before any of the rest of the crepes.

'Ganache' meant a very long time ago 'Idiot' in French and was made by accident. A young assistant of a pastry chef accidentally mixed cream and chocolate together. His chef got upset and yelled at him calling the mixture 'Ganache'. The chef tasted the mistake anyway and decided to use it for cakes.

Ganache is derived from the French word fool
So many comments hating on her pronunciation of "crepe"! Yes, it is not how you may pronounce the word, but that does not make it *wrong or bad* . It is simply the American English pronunciation of a French loanword. People bring words from other languages into their own all the time and pronunciation is adjusted to suit their mother tongue, and eventually it becomes common vocabulary. TACO. RAMEN. CURRY. PIZZA. All originally words from other languages that are now common words in not just American English, but many other languages around the world as well! So don't hate! Appreciate the sharing of cultures <3

Ganache used to mean dumb in the "old school" french. Legend says that the guy who "discovered" the ganache did it by pouring by mistake hot cream over chocolate, and his chef insulted him using that particular word. When he tasted the mix, the chef realized how tasty it is and named the mix accordingly: "La ganache"

Yo homebaker's experience here: resting crepe batter is important so the gluten strands in the batter can relax and not make the crepes chewy. Also, resting the batter allows the dry ingredients to fully hydrate; if you cooked the batter right away it'd be like cooking eggs on very very low heat (too liquidy and no structure).

I'd love to eat that cake! *heart eyes*  According to the French Wikipedia and its source the book 'Pierre HermÃ©, Le grand livre du chocolat : 380 recettes, Vevey, Mondo, 2007', the word "ganache" came from a mistake made by an apprentice chocolatier who dropped boiling cream in chocolate. His master immediately called him a "ganache", which meant "idiot" or "half-witted" back then. But when they discovered that what the apprentice had done was definitely edible, they called the sauce "ganache". But according to the ENGLISH Wikipedia and its source the 'Oxford English Dictionary', the name has its origins in a vaudeville from the 1860s.   Soooooo... what gives?
